text:
To be fair, I usually make recipes twice before I rate them as I seriously dislike reviewers who change, then rate the recipe vs making it as written first.  Good as written so I am rating this 4 stars for ease, time and ingredients usually on hand.  But for my family's preference I made the following modifications.  Used spiral noodles in place of egg noodles as they capture more sauce.  1/2 ground beef and 1/2 hot italian sausage which gave the casserole more complexity.  Used small pre-sliced pepperoni to save time.  Most importantly, this is a great casserole for making ahead ~ as with many pasta dishes, the flavor gets better the longer it sits.  Overall this is a great base recipe to build on.  Thank you Melissa for sharing!

Your basic recipe is good, but I use Kraft Mac and Cheese, make according to directions. Saute extra-lean ground beef with onion, green bell pepper, garlic.  Add two jars Ragu Pizza Quik, and two pkgs sliced Hormel Pepperoni, then bake as directed 350 for about 45 minutes. Yum. Is the most requested recipe by family, and at work. Delicious and easy for kids of all ages. Alison

text:
I really didn't have a whole lot of expectations for this dish, but actually loved it and so did the everyone else. I did read the many reviews about being dry and added a can of plain tomato sauce to the 15oz. pizza sauce, plus some fresh oregano and basil. I followed everything else except...I also added fresh mushrooms and black olives to meat mixture when cooking on the stove top. I used 16oz. mozzarella, and it filled a 10x15 perfectly. I did put half the meat/pasta/sauce mix in the bottom of casserole dish and then covered with a layer of cheese, reserving just a small amount for the top, and finished with the other half of pasta mix, cooked for 20 min as directed and then topped with the rest of moz. and some more pepperoni for looks and cooked for the additional ten min. I did top with some fresh cilantro & blk olives while steaming hot when I took it out of the oven...waited about ten min and cut so perfect. I will make again. Thanks. Everyone ate too much of this one.

text:
I always make a dish the way it is stated the first time and then usually make it again before I rate it. The first time this one was just barely above average for us, although we enjoyed it as a casual dinner.
The second time we agreed this was a 4 star with the the following changes: Reduced the ground beef to 1/4 lb, added 1/4 lb ground Italian sausage, and used a whole pack of pepperoni (7 oz) which is probably not quite two cups by volume. The pizza sauce we used was in a 14oz jar. Unlike other reviewers we thought that 14oz. was perfect. I have a feeling that most of those that want to use more sauce are probably using way more than 2 cups of "uncooked" noodles. We mixed 1/2 of the pepperoni in the mix and saved half for the top, then put the cheese on top of that. We thought this way was really good (for us) and will def. make it again.

text:
Awesome recipe! I changed it a bit based on previous reviews, and it turned out really good. All of my siblings and my parents really really liked it- it was also quite filling. Below is how I revised it (with 14 instead of 7 servings).

Instead of using egg noodles, I used spiral. Also, instead of using 4 cloves of garlic, I did a tsp. per clove of storebought minced garlic. I didn't use quite a whole onion. Instead of pepperoni, I chopped up some Summer Sausage that we had. I also added some fried pre-cooked bacon that I chopped into tidbits. Instead of using pizza sauce, I used Marinara sauce and added oregano. For the cheese, I added some cheddar and accidently stirred in the cheese along with everything else, but it turned out great.

Later on, I also discovered the dish tasted really good with sour cream, it doesn't make it quite so non-moist. Overall, love it!

OK - here's what I did - I used a box of wheat rotini pasta, 2 jars of pizza sauce, 1 lb hamburger meat browned with one chopped onion and garlic, 1 pack of turkey pepperoni (i took it out of the pack and quartered the whole pack).  pizza blend cheese and mozzarella cheese on top.  Used my big baking dish and threw it in the oven covered until it was bubbly- about 25 minutes- then uncovered and baked for about 5 more minutes.  YUMMO!!!!!  hubby and kiddos loved it!! served with french garlic bread.  Thanks for sharing this recipe!!!

text:
Great pasta!  I used sliced pepperoni chopped into small pieces, cooked with 1 lb. of grain-fed hamburger meat and a few garlic cloves.  I did use a little pizza sauce but didn't care for the flavor and instead used Newman's Own marinara, canned Dei Fratelli chopped italian tomatoes, herbs & olive oil, and a can of tomato paste.  I took others' recommendations and used egg noodles, which were fantastic!  Mixed in shredded mozzarella and topped with provolone, shredded farmer's cheese, and bits of mild cheddar.  Chose to use onion powder in place of actual onions and omitted the green peppers.  Turned out really good!  I would make this again.  :)

text:
I made this recipe 3x in a row in one week for different families.  ALL of the families raved about the casserole and are begging for the recipe.  My own family really liked this casserole, as well.

I did make some changes to the recipe based on other reviewers. 

Since I had to double the recipe to ensure lots of leftovers (and I used those very large foil baking pans for buffets) I tripled the noodles to 6 cups uncooked.  I doubled the lean ground beef to 1 lb. I still only used one onion and 1 bell pepper (did not double). I used 2 cups of sliced TURKEY pepperoni sausage (to keep it slightly leaner). I used 24 oz. of pizza sauce (jar and a half). Kept the amount of milk the same (1/4 cup).  And I tripled the amount of cheese to 3 cups.

I followed the recipe as is except I layered cheese in the middle (hence the need to triple the cheese amount to have enough for the middle layer and top layer).  Additionally I put in Italian Seasoning to the sauce to give it some spice.  I just eyeballed it.

That would be the only modification I would change.  I think the pizza sauce is bland without spices. I would try spagetti sauce instead to see if it adds more flavor.  

Because I doubled it I had to increase the cooking time to 40 minutes. 

This was a perfect dish for families who just had a baby.  It didn't have anything too spicy in it that would pose a problem to breastfeeding moms.  And the siblings loved it too!  It's a good comfort food and if you use lean meat, turkey pepp

We all loved this dish.  Lightened it up with 1 cup (2 oz) noodles (lightly crushed), part-skim mozzarella, and used 4 oz sweet Italian turkey sausage in place of the pepperoni.  Added 1 cup frozen (thawed) chopped spinach and 1 cup sliced mushrooms.  Baked, covered, at 400 degrees for 20 minutes, then uncovered and added cheese; cooked uncovered for the final 5 minutes.  A new favorite.  Thanks, Melissa.

Yummy and very easy to make.  I made a few changes, but as written, it would be 4 stars. 
I used bowtie pasta, because that's what I had on hand.  I added basil, white pepper, and salt to the sauce mixture.  I also doubled the cheese.  
Instead of mixing the pepperoni in with everything else, I layered it.  I poured half the mixture into my casserole dish, layered pepperoni and cheese, and then poured the rest of the mixture in, and layered more pepperoni and cheese on top.  It turned out fantastic, and I'll definitely be making this again.

LOVED this.  Ended up making a double batch (minus the noodles)... froze the second batch 'mixture' in a zip lock bag.  Plan to just boil the noodles, mix together and bake for a quick dinner on another night.  

Also - I did not include the milk as I didn't think it was necessary.  When I baked, I alternated layers of mixture and cheese.  Also did not 'add' the cheese for last 10 minutes, I just added it before I put it in the oven and did 1 cooking time (like a lasagna).  Served with a side salad and garlic bread.

text:
This casserole turned out delicious with just a few changes. First, I wanted a larger casserole, so I used more sauce and pasta. I omitted the hamburger and pepperoni (no one likes pepperoni). Instead I browned a pound of sweet Italian sausage with the onion and green pepper. I added 8 ounces of fresh mushrooms (sliced) and added that to the meat mixture toward the end of browning, then followed the rest of the recipe. I placed half of the mixture in the dish, put a layer of cheese, then the remainder of the pasta. Last 10 minutes of baking, I added a cup of cheese to the top and returned for baking until melted. It was very good.

text:
I prefer to make my pizza pasta with Italian Sausage or Johnsonville's new 3 cheese Italian Chicken sausage rather than ground beef.  It adds so much more flavor and who has plain ground beef on a pizza?  I've been making this for years as a potluck staple.  I never put green pepper in mine as I am allergic and some people don't like it.  I also add sliced black olives and mushrooms. If making for at home I will saute zucchini and add as well.  So start with this basic recipe (using rotini or penne pasta, not egg noodles) and tweak according to the tastes your family likes.  Also adding  a little Italian seasoning goes a long way.

My husband and I are pizza lovers so I thought I'd try this out since it seemed creative and delicious and it was. We both really liked it, I made some alterations though. Neither of us like green pepper so I didn't add those and I only used half an onion since a whole one seemed like it would be too much and I was right, there was plenty of onion when I made it with only half. I also put Garlic salt on the meat,onion, and minced garlic mixture while cooking. It was good that first time but it wasn't cheesy enough for my hubby and I since we are cheese lovers so the second time I made it I added a cup of cheddar cheese into the mixture of sauce, noodles, etc before putting it into the oven. I think next time I will double the batch since this is only enough for an 8x8 casserole dish. Next time I'll use a 9x13 casserole dish, that way there are leftovers because I wanted more both times lol. Overall this will be a great addition to the list of recipes I make for us because it's great!

text:
Very good basic recipe. Definitely beats out a box type dinner, if you make those. I added a can of mushrooms and a little cheese in with the mixture as well as the amount on top. I'd suggest adding some additional seasoning such as Marjoram or Basil and maybe some fennel seed. I used turkey pepperoni to save calories and reduce any additional grease and no one even noticed. I also added 1/4lb Italian sausage into the hamburger mixture which gave some additional flavor (be sure to drain off grease!). Made the night before, so I increased the time in the oven before adding the cheese as it needed it in order to heat through after being refrigerated. All in all, an easy Sunday night dinner.

I made this for my family tonight. I like to cook meals that will reheat nicely so I can have a quick easy lunch for a few days. This would have been great for that IF there had been any leftovers. This was a huge hit with my family. Only person that did not like it was my younger brother who is going through a phase where he doesn't want anything unfamiliar. He thought I was making regular pizza, so he was disappointed. But everyone else loved it. My 1 year old sister was lurching towards her bowl. We couldn't keep the bites coming fast enough.

I used a little more cheese than it called for. Maybe around a cup and a half. I also added some mushrooms and used mini pepperoni instead of the full sized pepperoni. This was a quick easy meal and it's absolutely delicious. I will definitely make this one again!!

text:
I was looking for something to do with my Pizza night leftovers because I ended up buying too much pizza sauce and had leftover toppings like black olives, mushrooms and pepperonis. 
Due to making this as a leftover-user, I made the following changes:
-I used pre-sliced pepperonis and cut them into fours
-I used no-yolk egg noodles
-I added more mushrooms and black olives (I see others did this as well)
-I used spicy chicken sausage in lieu of ground beef (I have a no-beef family member)
-I lastly topped with BOTH mozzarella and parmesan because I had it
Basically this turned out delicious. I only gave it 4 stars because it is so high in grease and fat that after eating TWO large servings, I got a stomach ache! But I guess that isn't the recipes fault!!!

text:
Excellent! Use the egg noodles, penne, rotini, and rigatoni are just not the same.  This recipe can easily be doubled and baked in a lasagne pan, go easy on the onion.  The beauty of this recipe is that you can use any of your favorite pizza toppings.  You can brown up to two pounds of loose hot or sweet sausage with some good baked ham. Pepper rings, black olives, thick sliced pepperoni (halved), mushrooms, if you like that sort of thing. I used 4 cups of Italian cheese blend.  Saved some ingredients for a topping, threw on top after 40 minutes, baked an additional 5-10.  Thanks Melissa!  Again, use the egg noodles, you're not making baked ziti.

text:
Just made this recipe for dinner tonite...so much easier than actual homemade pizza!  And, I already had all the ingredients on hand, which was a plus also.  I fixed one pan "supreme style" - this one was 13x9 pan with rotini noodles, pizza sauce, hamburger, sausage, pepperoni, onions, mushrooms and black olives. The smaller pan was "pepperoni only" which left out everything except the pepperoni, hamburger, sausage and cheese for my picky daughter, who said her version was"the bomb".  The rest of us also loved the fully-loaded version....I forgot to add the garlic - probably would've made it even better....and I didn't add the milk.  I used 3 jars of pizza quick sauce, 1 lb hamburger, 1 lb pork sausage, 1 pkg pepperoni, 4 cups shredded mozzarella which I layered between the pasta in the pans. I also used a large can of mushrooms, 1 large onion, and 1 can chopped black olives with 1 box rotini noodles. It made a full 13x9 pan, plus a small brownie pan of the pasta.  We all loved it, and it was a quick and filling meal.  Next time I will remember to add the garlic, and dice up a small amount of the green pepper (it was the only thing I didn't already have).   I have added this recipe to my "keeper" book.  Thanks so much for sharing it!!

text:
OK, so...to preface this...I can't eat gluten (wheat) and I'm allergic to dairy...so I didn't make this recipe exactly as written. I used rice milk instead of regular milk, I used brown rice pasta instead of egg noodles, and I omitted the cheese. It was still pretty decent. I baked it covered with aluminum foil so that it would stay moist since I didn't have cheese. It could definitely use more sauce - I think it would need more sauce even if I had the cheese. I saw that some people said that it was just like spaghetti. I guess does kind of have that type of flavor, but I associate pizza sauce with pizza, so anything with pizza sauce tastes pizza-y to me. Use real "pizza sauce" if you want it to taste like pizza, not just tomato sauce. Also, you could add some extra uncooked pizza sauce at the end..pizza sauce loses a little bit of the pizza-ness when it gets cooked into the noodles.

My daughter said it tastes like the pizza topping that falls off. Yummy.

I read the reviews saying it was bland so I tweaked this recipe a little. First, I used rotini, like in the picture, instead of egg noodles. Less to say it was absolutely delicious and we will be making this again.

I made a very similar version of this recipe for freezer dinners and  it was a huge success with the whole family.  You can add or subtract what meats/veggies you like or don't like. Just remember to take it out of the freezer and place in the refrigerator the night before and you have a great go to meal.  Beats fast food any time.

Love Love LOVE IT! I made it tonight and I'm typing this as I'm trying to savor my serving. I could eat the whole pan. I tweaked it a teeny bit. I added mild italian sausage and didn't use any milk, I didn't see any need for the milk. I layered the cheese and pepperoni on top like a regular pizza. I think the brand of pizza sauce makes all the difference for the people that said it was bland. I used Classico Traditional Pizza Sauce which was delicious on it's own and seasoned my meat before adding it in with everything else. The kids gobbled it up like it was their last meal which is amazing because they don't normally eat pepperoni pizza but they were licking their bowls by the end of it lol. Two thumbs up, 10 stars, so many possibilities!

text:
My mother used to make this all the time growing up and we loved it! The differences are I use Rotini noodles instead of egg noodles as egg noodles have to soft and soggy of a texture for my taste in this sort of recipe. I also add a half jar of spaghetti sauce, whatever flavor I feel at the time because it seemed too dry without it. I also omit the peppers because my hubby doesn't like them. And I add cheese to the casserole mix with all the other ingredients before baking it. Goes great with a side of garlic bread or toast!

I don't normally deviate from recipes, particularly not ones that are this popular.  I made this as written.....until right before I baked it. I took a cue from Chef John's mac & cheese. The part of that dish I received the most compliments on was the bread crumb topping, so I added one to this dish. text:
This was tasty!  I know I have a winner recipe on my hands when my toddler can't have enough!  My husband went back for seconds, so that's another compliment.  I swapped a few things to my liking and with what I had on hand.  I used elbow macaroni and I had almost exactly 1 cup of Mexican blend cheese left that I needed to use up.  Delish.  I decided to skip on the ground beef because we don't like it on pizzas and it doesn't add much flavor unseasoned anyway.  We prefer sweet italian sausage on our pizza, so next time I get my hands on those I may put those in instead.  Also, I got a great idea from my husband because I told him I had a problem with the pepperoni sticking together as I mixed everything and he said layer it like a lasagna.  I will definitely try that next time!  Last thing, I got carried away having fun doing this and I added the cheese before baking it, lol, but no worries.  If you have this problem, just put some aluminum foil over the pasta, cook the 20 minutes, uncover then cook for the 5 minutes extra and it's just fine.  Thanks for the recipe Melissa!

text:
This was pretty good! Here's what I did: I browned 1 lb. ground beef in the skillet, along with pepperoni slices that I quartered. Once nice & brown, drained the skillet,put the meat back in,  added in 1 tsp. olive oil and chopped onion, 1 tbsp. dried oregano,1 tbsp. red pepper flakes, kosher salt to taste, 1 tsp. ground black pepper,  and 4 cloves of chopped garlic. Let that sautee a few minutes. Then, I stirred in 16 oz. of jarred Ragu Pizza Quik. Mixed well and let it simmer while I cooked the pasta. Once pasta was done, I drained it and added it to the skillet with the pizza mixture. Added in 4 tbsp. of milk and stirred again. In my baking dish, I put half the pasta/meat mixture, a generous helping of Kraft pizza style shredded cheese, and then added the rest of the pasta/meat mixture. I topped with another generous helping of mozaarella, and then topped it with whole pepperoni slices. Finally, I took a block of romano and lightly grated it over the pepperoni. Baked for 30 minutes til bubbly and brown and it was very tasty.

text:
This is a good recipe as written.  I adapted it by changing from pepperoni to Italian sausage, red onion, and kept the green pepper.  I cooked these up in a skillet and added some garlic and some oregano and crushed red pepper.  I used a 1lb can of spaghetti sauce and rotini pasta.  Finally I took a package of Italian cheeses and mixed half the bag in the casserole and baked for 30 minutes.  Then remove from the oven and stir, otherwise the pasta on top has a tendency to not cook and be crunchy.  Cook for another 30 minutes.  Top with remaining cheese and cook until cheese is melted about 10 minutes.

text:
This recipe was Great.  I did add a little to it.  I used 1 pound lean ground beef, 1 jimmy dean sage flavor sausage. I used 2 green peppers, 1 large onion, I also added Italian Seasoning, 2 cloves minced garlic and pepper.  I browned all together, then drained.  For Pasta I used a mixture of Rotini and Piccolini (mini wheels)for my little guy. I also added 3 jars 14 ounce each of pizza sauce, 1 whole bag of pepperoni, and 8 tablespoons of milk.  After mixing all ingredients together, I put it into a 13x9 pan.  I sprayed with pam, for easy cleanup.  I put into oven for 25-30 minutes, then added 3 cups of pizza cheese and parmesan cheese.  I kept it in until the cheese was a little brown.  I removed from oven and let set for 10 minutes. I had mushrooms, black olives, and extra fixins on the side so my family could add what they liked. My hubby and toddler loved it.  I made enough for tomorrows dinner.  This is a great dish to do that with, especially with a busy day ahead.

I might try one reveiwers idea next time with using Italian sausage. Also cooked the pepperoni a little bit before adding it to the mixture; just to get some of the grease out of it.

text:
I made this tonite and it was really good.  Kind of a shortcut lasagna, in a way.  I used nearly 4 cups (dry measure) egg noodles-I used the twisty shaped ones.  I also added some more sauce, and it was a zesty/spicy variety.  In addition, I doubled the cheese and mixed half of it within the pasta/sauce/meat mix and put the other half on top.  I sliced up 7 brown mushrooms and sauteed them before adding to the mix.  I put everything in a 9X13 glass pan and baked.  Very good.  I can see how some people thought it was bland, but thanks to the zesty spicy tomato sauce I used, mine was quite flavorful.  I might add green peppers next time, but otherwise, it was plenty meaty with the ground beef and pepperoni slices.  Perfect for a cold nite!

text:
So, first of all I think ratings should be based on a recipe's uniqueness and idea. Potentially there are millions of people who will try this recipe in time and as many people who try this recipe there will potentially be that many different individual tastes. For example, I added more ingredients than the recipe called for and the picture looked like it added more ingredients, i.e., sliced black olives (which I love) and basil as a topper (which my wife really loves!). I also read other reviewers' comments and incorporated some of their ideas. Oh and the person who suggested shrooms; great idea, but I used fresh. I wanted to keep it simple but maybe next time I'll make my own marinara sauce (Apparently I don't like commercially prepared sauces). Lastly, I urge anyone who cooks with mozzarella cheese to use a high quality cheese. It's best to buy fully hydrated mozzarella but that is a lengthy process to remove the water; therefore buy the market prepackaged block mozzarella and shred it yourself (much better outcome).

Final thoughts: The way I made it didn't taste much like pizza even though I added Deli-style pepperoni but it was a great 
meat marinara pasta on steroids.

Thanks for the idea!

text:
I love pizza so any variation on that is something I'm willing to try. I used spiral pasta to hold more sauce per bite. I used 1/4lb hot Italian sausage and 1/4lb lean ground beef. I did not use onion or green pepper. I used 1 small can portabella pieces that I added before I baked. I put a layer of mozzerella in the middle before I baked and the required mozzerella on top for the last 10 minutes. For sauce I used Hunt's basil, garlic, oregano tomato sauce. I also left out the garlic as there was garlic in my sauce. This dish was a hit at Thanksgiving

I may try it again with at least double the sauce and a shorter baking time since really all of the ingredients are cooked before baking anyway.

text:
This is a quick and EASY dish, and it gets an enthusiastic TWO THUMBS UP from Hubby, who is the cook in the house. You can make this recipe as-is and it will be fine, so my 5-stars is based on the original recipe not my personal preferences in tweaking this recipe. :::::::  I knew my Hubby is a serious meat/cheese fanatic, so I added the entire pack of pepperoni (that I cut up) and doubled the cheese. For me it was a bit much as far as the add'l pepperoni, but Hubby went crazy over it. I cooked the pepperoni along with the ground beef.  I apparently didn't read the recipe close enough and went ahead and stirred my 8-oz pk of cheese in with the pizza sauce mixture. (Turned out fine.) I put the meat mixture into the casserole dish in two portions so that I could sandwich the add'l 8-oz pk of mozzarella layered in between. The good news is you can tweak this quick and easy recipe to suit your particular desire.

I made this yesterday with some adjustments. I used whole wheat penne pasta. Instead of beef, I used extra lean ground turkey which I seasoned with onion powder, pepper, oregano, minced garlic, and about 1 or 2 tsp of ground Chile de Arbol. Once ready to be mixed together, I used half turkey pepperoni and half regular pepperoni. Also, I sprinkled about 1/2-3/4 cup of cheese in the mixture and added less cheese on top, but still enough to taste the cheese. Sliced tomatoes were placed on the top. On my boyfriend's half I added black olives, mushrooms, and jalepenos, plus a sprinkle of Chile de Arbol on the top. It was delicious. My boyfriend especially loved it. He ate basically his hole half (3 bowls full) to the point he said his stomach hurt. :P It was definitely a hit.

text:
LOVE!  Thank you so much for such a great, easy recipe.  My picky 6-year old absolutely loved this dish.  I modified it for a gluten-free/dairy-free diet by using Tinkyada spiral shells (I've tried other GF brands and Tinkyada is by far the best), omitting the 4 T of milk and using a dairy-free cheese, such as the Daiya mozzarella shreds- came out fantastic!  I read where a previous reviewer expressed their doubts whether a 14 oz. jar of pizza sauce would be enough or not- I thought the same thing but sure enough, the 14 oz. is just the right amount!  Not dry or swamped with too much sauce.  I also used Italian ground sausage instead of beef.  The best thing about this recipe is that you can customize it the way you want, much like ordering a regular pizza.  Thanks again for sharing!

I am eating the left-overs right now :)

None
text:
This is a great go-to recipe, one that everybody likes, and is very easy to throw together.  I use rotini instead of egg noodles, because I find that they stand up to stirring better and hold more flavor than the recommended egg noodles.  I also quartered the pepperoni, as I found the slices tend to "spoon" together and end up stuck together in stacks in various places about the casserole.  Like most other casseroles, this can be assembled whenever you have time and stored in the fridge until ready to bake - just add on about 5-10 minutes to the baking time.  Thanks for the recipe, Melissa!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was a very tasty, easy recipe to make.  However, I did make a few adjustments to "rev." up the flavor a bit to our liking and preferences:  I used rotini noodles in lieu of the egg noodles (they clump less); I used 1/2 pound hot Italian sausage in lieu of the ground beef; I used four cloves of garlic; I omitted the bell pepper (we don't get it on our pizzas); I sliced the pepperoni pieces in half for better blending in the casserole and used Turkey pepperoni to cut the fat;  I used almost 3/4 of a 32 ounce jar of pizza sauce (I don't like my pasta casseroles dry); and probably closer to 6 oz. of shredded Italian cheese blend in lieu of mozzarella.  It was yummy!  Will definitely make again!
Review:
Rating:
5

text:
I am giving this four stars, because to make it five stars I had to adjust the recipe.  I added black olives, mushrooms, mozzarella cheese, fresh grated parmesan cheese, and sharp cheddar cheese, and Chef Paul Prudhomme's Herbal Pizza & Pasta Magic seasoning blend.   I did use 1/2 lb ground beef, approx. 4 oz of pepperoni slices quartered, 4 3/4 cups cooked elbow macaroni, 26 oz. can of Classico Italian sausage pasta sauce, 1/2 can of diced tomatoes (that I processed till smooth) and approx 1/3 cup milk.  I kinda eyeballed the liquids ( I make casseroles often and can kinda know when they have enough liquid).  I followed the directions and then mixed everything together in a big bowl.  I seasoned extra well Herbal seasoning and salt, onion powder, and garlic powder as well.  I mixed in one cup of mozzarella, 3/4 cup cheddar, and 1/2 cup fresh grated parmesan cheese as well as most of the olives and mushrooms.  I baked in 2 1/2 qt casserole and a 1 1/2 qt casserole dish ( yes, it made a ton of casserole)for 50 minutes until it was bubbling in the middle.  I added 1 cup of mozzarella and 1/2 cup of cheddar mixed together on the top.  Then I sprinkled with some onion, bellpepper, olives, mushrooms and whole pepperoni slices I set aside for the top of the casserole. Put in over for about 7 minutes until cheese was melted.  I swear this was the best casserole I have made yet.  My husband kept saying "Will you please move this pot so I won't get anymore!!!!"  I am pregnant and have

text:
Fantastic.  I use homemade marinara sauce rather than pizza sauce and ground turkey rather than beef (you would never know the difference).  While I was making this, I kept thinking that it wasn't going to be enough pasta and way too much of the other ingredients, but the proportions were actually quite nice.  I also use 2 cups of cheese.  I layer half the mixture in the dish, then sprinkle with 1 cup cheese, then add the other half of the mixture, then bake as directed.  I add the other cup of cheese after 20 minutes, bake for 5 minutes, then broil for a few minutes to give it that nice crunchy, browned top.

This has been my husband's favorite dish so far. While I was browning the meat I added garlic. text:
This recipe was great!  I used ground chicken instead of beef, and added mushrooms to make it a true combination style pizza casserole.  I had more meat than the recipe called for so I scaled up the noodles, the sauce and the milk.  The mushrooms made up for not scaling up the green pepper and the amount of pepperoni the recipe called for was perfect, even for the larger casserole.  I also used more cheese because my husband and I are cheese lovers.  Definitely a keeper and leftovers can be frozen for lunches.  Thanks Melissa.
